  <article>
    <p class="categories"></p>
    <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956117/acer-iconia-tab-a510-now-available-ics-update-a500-a100">Acer Iconia Tab A510 now on sale, Android 4.0 rolls out to earlier Acer tablets on April 27</a></h2>
    
    <div class="byline clearfix">
      <div class="floatL">
        <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/Sean%20Hollister" class="author">Sean Hollister</a>
        April  17, 2012 08:57 pm
      </div>
      
        <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956117/acer-iconia-tab-a510-now-available-ics-update-a500-a100#comments" class="comment-count  heat1">8</a></div>
      
    </div>
    <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956117/acer-iconia-tab-a510-now-available-ics-update-a500-a100'>
      <div class="shadowbox">
        <img alt="Acer Iconia Tab A510" class="article-image" height="200" src="http://cdn3.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3740464/acer-iconia-tab-a510-verge-007_gallery_post_large_medium.jpg" width="300" />
      </div>
    </a>

    <p>And then there were two: if we're counting correctly, Acer's Iconia Tab A510 just became the second quad-core Tegra 3 tablet to go on sale in the United States. While it doesn't have an optional keyboard dock like the <a href="http://www.theverge.com/products/eee-pad-transformer-prime-tf201/3279">Asus Transformer Prime</a>, the 10.1-inch Android 4.0 slate does have a fairly sleek design, 32GB of storage and a sizable 9800mAh battery pack to its name, and &mdash; assuming you're not holding out <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/3/29/2910731/nvidia-ceo-predicts-199-tegra-3-tablets-by-summer">for a $199 Tegra 3</a> &mdash; you can pick it up for $449.99 at Acer's website today. </p>
<p>If you're not ready for the latest and greatest, though, you'd probably be happy to hear that Acer's existing dual-core Iconia Tab A500 and A100 tablets will be getting <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/2/16/2801228/acer-iconia-tab-a100-a500-android-4-0-april">an update to Android 4.0</a> quite soon. Assuming you aren't already running <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/2/22/2818025/android-4-0-leak-acer-iconia-tab-a100-a500">a leaked version of the Ice Cream Sandwich update</a>, a support page at Acer says that the legitimate builds of the...</p>

    
      <quote class="big">
        <span><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956117/acer-iconia-tab-a510-now-available-ics-update-a500-a100">Another 10-inch quad-core option for Android tablet buyers</a></span>
        
      </quote>
    
    
    
  </article>
</div>

  <article>
    <p class="categories"></p>
    <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956010/windows-phone-apollo-upgrade">All Windows Phones to get upgrade to 'next major version,' according to Microsoft developer evangelist (update)</a></h2>
    
    <div class="byline clearfix">
      <div class="floatL">
        <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/Dieter%20Bohn" class="author">Dieter Bohn</a>
        April  17, 2012 08:07 pm
      </div>
      
        <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956010/windows-phone-apollo-upgrade#comments" class="comment-count  heat4">84</a></div>
      
    </div>
    <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956010/windows-phone-apollo-upgrade'>
      <div class="shadowbox">
        <img alt="Samsung Focus Flash and Focus S" class="article-image" height="200" src="http://cdn3.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3740223/Samsung-Focus-S-Flash-Pictures-hands-on-DSC_0014-rm-verge-1000_large_medium.jpg" width="300" />
      </div>
    </a>

    <p>According to an interview that Microsoft developer evangelist <a target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/#!/nuno_ms">Nuno Silva</a> gave to <i><a target="_blank" href="http://portal.zwame.pt/27496/artigo/entrevista-a-nuno-silva-evangelista-da-microsoft-para-o-windows-phone-em-portugal">Zwame</a></i>, every Windows Phone sold to date should be getting the upgrade to the next "major version of Windows Phone." Silva further made it clear that he wasn't just referring to current devices, but also the first-generation of Windows Phone devices going back to the Omnia 7. Presumably, the "major" here isn't a...</p>

    
      <quote class="big">
        <span><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2956010/windows-phone-apollo-upgrade">"All actual devices will get upgrade to the next major version of Windows Phone."</a></span>
        
          <em>Microsoft developer evangelist Nuno Silva</em>
        
      </quote>
    
    
    
  </article>
</div>

  <article>
    <p class="categories"></p>
    <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955075/pew-internet-mobile-nfc-payments-2020">NFC payments could dominate commerce by 2020, according to study</a></h2>
    
    <div class="byline clearfix">
      <div class="floatL">
        <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/AndrewRWebster" class="author">Andrew Webster</a>
        April  17, 2012 07:33 pm
      </div>
      
        <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955075/pew-internet-mobile-nfc-payments-2020#comments" class="comment-count  heat2">11</a></div>
      
    </div>
    <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955075/pew-internet-mobile-nfc-payments-2020'>
      <div class="shadowbox">
        <img alt="Google Wallet NFC taxi contactless payment (1020" class="article-image" height="200" src="http://cdn3.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3736532/google-wallet-nfc-taxi_1020_large_medium.jpg" width="300" />
      </div>
    </a>

    <p>While mobile payment solutions like Google Wallet are only starting to catch on, a new study suggests that by 2020 they could become the dominant form of payment. The study &mdash; conducted by the Pew Internet &amp; American Life Project and Elon University's Imagining the Internet Center &mdash; surveyed a total of 1,021 "internet experts and other internet users." It found that 65 percent of those who...</p>

    <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955583/marudai-bulletproof-iphone-case">Bulletproof case keeps your iPhone safe for $650</a></h2>
    
    <div class="byline clearfix">
      <div class="floatL">
        <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/AndrewRWebster" class="author">Andrew Webster</a>
        April  17, 2012 08:02 pm
      </div>
      
        <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955583/marudai-bulletproof-iphone-case#comments" class="comment-count  heat3">25</a></div>
      
    </div>
    <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955583/marudai-bulletproof-iphone-case'>
      <div class="shadowbox">
        <img alt="Marudai bulletproof phone" class="article-image" height="200" src="http://cdn1.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3738595/info-product-001_large_medium.jpeg" width="300" />
      </div>
    </a>

    <p>Japanese firm Marudai has unveiled a new iPhone 4 case that turns your delicate smartphone into a bulletproof slab of metal. For &yen;52,500 ($650), the case adds a 1-inch thick layer of steel to protect the back of your phone, while the front (excluding the screen) is covered with machined aluminum. The manufacturer claims that the case can withstand a .50 caliber bullet. Of course, the added protection comes with a price &mdash; namely the fact that your phone will be big enough to put the Galaxy Note to shame, as the case measures in at 138 x 81.8 x 39.6 millimeters and weighs 2.1 kilograms...</p>

    
    
    
  </article>
</div>

  <article>
    <p class="categories"></p>
    <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955461/america-social-media-healthcare-survey">One-third of Americans using social media to share health information, survey finds</a></h2>
    
    <div class="byline clearfix">
      <div class="floatL">
        <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/adirobertson" class="author">Adi Robertson</a>
        April  17, 2012 06:49 pm
      </div>
      
        <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955461/america-social-media-healthcare-survey#comments" class="comment-count  heat1">5</a></div>
      
    </div>
    <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955461/america-social-media-healthcare-survey'>
      <div class="shadowbox">
        <img alt="Twitter Stethoscope Box" class="article-image" height="200" src="http://cdn1.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3738520/20120417-16591669-twitterscope-IMG_0869_large_JPG_medium.jpg" width="300" />
      </div>
    </a>

    <p>Doctors may be rightfully skeptical of internet-based diagnoses, but patients are increasingly using social media in a variety of other ways when they get sick. A survey of about 1,000 US adults by consulting house PwC Health Industries found that a third of them had shared health information or solicited advice through social media, including Facebook and Twitter. As you might expect, that number was far higher for younger adults: 80 percent of those 18 to 24 said they would be willing to share health information over social media (even if they hadn't necessarily done it), compared to 45 percent of those 45 to 64. Even so, that's a large...</p>

    
    
    
  </article>

  <div class="storybox top grid_8">
    <article class="clearfix">
      <div class="article-content">
        <p class="categories"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/label/report">Report</a></p>
        <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955591/larry-page-on-the-stand-oracle-dispute-we-didnt-do-anything-wrong">Larry Page on the stand in Oracle trial: 'We didn't do anything wrong'</a></h2>
        <div class="byline clearfix">
          <div class="floatL">
            <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/bcbishop" class="author">Bryan Bishop</a>
            April  17, 2012 06:36 pm
          </div>
          
            <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955591/larry-page-on-the-stand-oracle-dispute-we-didnt-do-anything-wrong#comments" class="comment-count heat5">169</a></div>
          
        </div>
        <p>Oracle and Google's legal fight has finally <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2954854/oracle-roadmap-infringement-case-against-google">made its way to the courtroom</a>, with Oracle CEO <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955445/oracle-ceo-considered-rim-palm-purchase/in/2709577">Larry Ellison taking the stand earlier this morning</a>.   <div class="storybox top grid_8">
    <article class="clearfix">
      <div class="article-content">
        <p class="categories"></p>
        <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955382/amazon-appstore-code-obfuscation-cloning">Amazon shows developers how to obscure code to avoid cloning</a></h2>
        <div class="byline clearfix">
          <div class="floatL">
            <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/AndrewRWebster" class="author">Andrew Webster</a>
            April  17, 2012 05:07 pm
          </div>
          
            <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955382/amazon-appstore-code-obfuscation-cloning#comments" class="comment-count heat1">7</a></div>
          
        </div>
        <p>Mobile apps are no stranger to <a href="http://www.theverge.com/gaming/2012/2/22/2810409/cloning-wars-vlambeer-vs-gamenauts">issues of cloning</a>, and Amazon is trying to help developers avoid having their work copied by advising them to obfuscate their code. In a post on its <a href="http://www.amazonappstoredev.com/2012/04/code-obfuscation-for-the-amazon-in-app-purchasing-api.html" target="_blank">developer blog</a>, Amazon provides a quick walkthrough to show developers how to go about modifying their code so that...</p>
        
      </div>
      <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955382/amazon-appstore-code-obfuscation-cloning'>
        <div class='article-image shadowbox image-window shadowbox' style='height:225px; width:300px;'>
  <img alt="Kindle Fire Amazon Appstore" src="http://cdn2.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3737839/kindle-tablet-soft-012_gallery_post_large_large.jpg" style="position: absolute; top: -12.5px; left: 0px;" width="300" />
  
</div>

      </a>
    </article>
  </div>


  
  <div class="storybox right grid_4">
    <article>
      <p class="categories"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/label/hands--on">Hands-on</a><a href="http://www.theverge.com/label/video">Video</a></p>
      <h2 class="title"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955453/padcaster-ipad-camera-accessory-hands-on">Padcaster iPad case: add DSLR glass to your tablet's camera (hands-on)</a></h2>
      
      <div class="byline clearfix">
        <div class="floatL">
          <a href="http://www.theverge.com/users/piercedavid" class="author">David Pierce</a>
          April  17, 2012 04:54 pm
        </div>
        
          <div class="floatR"><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955453/padcaster-ipad-camera-accessory-hands-on#comments" class="comment-count heat2">19</a></div>
        
      </div>
      <a href='http://www.theverge.com/2012/4/17/2955453/padcaster-ipad-camera-accessory-hands-on'>
        <div class='article-image shadowbox image-window shadowbox' style='height:225px; width:300px;'>
  <img alt="Padcaster hands-on" src="http://cdn0.sbnation.com/entry_photo_images/3738355/_MFC9593-hero_large_large.jpg" style="position: absolute; top: -12.5px; left: 0px;" width="300" />
  
</div>

      </a>
      <p>The iPad's a great tool for editing and sharing video, and the new model even has <a href="http://www.theverge.com/2012/3/14/2870533/ipad-review#section_5">an excellent camera</a>, but without multiple lenses, or a tripod mount it's not as usable or versatile as dedicated video cameras. The Padcaster aims to change that: it's a sturdy case that lets you connect your tablet to a tripod and a lens, and turn it into a one-step solution for recording, editing, and sharing video. The $199 device...</p>
    </article>
  </div>
